1 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Valencia


No. CR-16-0156-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


241 Ariz. 206; 386 P.3d 392; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 335; 754 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



December 23, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Valencia v. Ariz., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 6914 (U.S., Nov. 27, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable James E. Marner, Judge. The Honorable Catherine M. Woods, Judge. Nos. CR048232 and CR051447. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 239 Ariz. 255, 370 P.3d 124 (App. 2016) [***1] .
State v. Valencia, 239 Ariz. 255, 370 P.3d 124, 2016 Ariz. App. LEXIS 44 (Ariz. Ct. App., Mar. 28, 2016)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, REVERSED AND REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Petitioners, who received natural life sentences for homicides committed as juveniles, were entitled to evidentiary hearings on their Ariz. R. Crim. P. 32.1(g) petitions for post-conviction relief because they made colorable claims for relief based on Miller v. Alabama, which held that imposing a sentence of life without parole on a child whose crime reflects transient immaturity violates the Eighth Amendment; [2]-Miller represented a clear break from the past for purposes of rule 32.1(g); [3]-Arizona law, when petitioners were sentenced, allowed a trial court to impose a natural life sentence on a juvenile convicted of first degree murder without distinguishing crimes that reflected irreparable corruption rather than the transient immaturity of youth; [4]-Because Miller reflected a new substantive rule of constitutional law, the rule was given retroactive effect.


OUTCOME: The opinion of the court of appeals was vacated, the trial court's rulings dismissing the petitions for post-conviction relief were reversed, and the cases were remanded for further proceedings.

3 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Hall v. Elected Officials' Ret. Plan


No. CV-15-0180-T/AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


241 Ariz. 33; 383 P.3d 1107; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 307; 751 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 18



November 10, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Randall H. Warner, Judge. No. CV2011-021234.
Hall v. Elected Officials' Ret. Plan, 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 196 (Ariz., June 11, 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED IN PART AND REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The senate bill's change to the benefit increased formula violated the Pension Clause of the Arizona Constitution, Ariz. Const. art. 29, § 1, because it diminished and impaired the pension benefits of the members of the Arizona Elected Officials' Retirement Plan; [2]-The bill's changes to the benefit increased formula and the contribution rate violated Yeazell because the Arizona Legislature could not unilaterally change the terms of the members' pension contracts once their rights to those terms vested at the beginning of the members' employment; [3]-The trial court erred in not awarding attorney fees to the members pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-341.01(A) because the Plan's relationship with the members was governed by the members' employment contracts with the State of Arizona.


OUTCOME: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.

 

4 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Holle


No. CR-15-0348-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


240 Ariz. 300; 379 P.3d 197; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 260; 747 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



September 13, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Holle v. Arizona, 197 L. Ed. 2d 650, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 2286 (U.S., Apr. 3, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Richard D. Nichols, Judge. No. CR20131185-001. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 238 Ariz. 218, 358 P.3d 639 (App. 2015) [***1] .
State v. Holle, 238 Ariz. 218, 358 P.3d 639, 2015 Ariz. App. LEXIS 197 (Ariz. Ct. App., Sept. 16, 2015)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a prosecution under Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-1404(A), -1410(A), the court properly instructed the jury that defendant's alleged lack of sexual motivation was an affirmative defense, requiring him to prove by a preponderance of the evidence that he was not motivated by a sexual interest; under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1407(E), lack of sexual motivation is an affirmative defense under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-103(A), (B) that the defendant must prove, and thus the State need not prove as an element of those crimes that the defendant's conduct was motivated by a sexual interest.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed and opinion vacated.

 

5 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Premier Physicians Grp., PLLC v. Navarro


No. CV-15-0323-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


240 Ariz. 193; 377 P.3d 988; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 222; 746 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 29



August 30, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: No. CV2014-090145. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Mark F. Aceto, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 238 Ariz. 156, 357 P.3d 840 (App. 2015) [***1] .
Premier Physicians Grp., PLLC v. Navarro, 238 Ariz. 156, 357 P.3d 840, 2015 Ariz. App. LEXIS 256 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2015)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The legislature intended Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-932(A) to require non-hospital providers to record liens before services were first provided or within 30 days thereafter; hence, the physician group's lien was not timely recorded and the trial court properly dismissed its claim against defendants; [2]-Because the group was no longer the prevailing party, it was not entitled to attorney fees; [3]-Defendants were entitled to costs and were awarded attorney fees as the prevailing parties under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 33-934(B).


OUTCOME: Judgment of court of appeals vacated; trial court's judgment affirmed.

 

6 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. Tamburri


No. CV-16-0143-AP/EL


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


240 Ariz. 126; 377 P.3d 323; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 205; 746 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



August 26, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable John R. Hannah, Jr., Judge. No. CV2016-008547.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because appellant did not show that Arizona's signature requirements, either facially or as applied to him, would prevent reasonably diligent minor party candidates from gaining ballot access, the requirements did not severely burden the ability of candidates to exercise their U.S. Const. amend. I rights; Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 16-321 and 16-322 did not require that Libertarians allow non-party members to vote in their primary, but merely required that a Libertarian candidate for U.S. Senate obtain sufficient signatures from voters registered with either his party or with no other recognized party; [2]-The 0.25 percent signature requirement in § 16-322 was rationally related to the State of Arizona's legitimate interest in ensuring that candidates who appeared on the general election ballot had some significant modicum of support.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

7 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gray


No. CR-15-0293-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


239 Ariz. 475; 372 P.3d 999; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 161



June 20, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Scott Rash, Judge. No. CR20132758-001 Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two 238 Ariz. 147, 357 P.3d 831 (App. 2015) [***1] .
State v. Gray, 238 Ariz. 147, 357 P.3d 831, 2015 Ariz. App. LEXIS 145 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2015)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The superior court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's requested entrapment instruction because he did not affirmatively admit to the substantial elements of the offense charged, as required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-206(A); defendant could not invoke the affirmative defense merely by declining to challenge the State's evidence, even when it included incriminating statements made by him to the undercover officer.


OUTCOME: Judgment of court of appeals vacated; superior court judgment affirmed.

 

8 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Goudeau


No. CR-11-0406-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


239 Ariz. 421; 372 P.3d 945; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 160



June 17, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: AMENDED BY ORDER FILED JULY 5, 2016
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Goudeau v. Ariz., 196 L. Ed. 2d 172, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 6021 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Warren J. Granville, Judge. No. CR2007-005449.
State v. Goudeau, 2009 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 833 (2009)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a capital murder prosecution, no Sixth Amendment confrontation error resulted when defendant was denied the opportunity to observe or participate in the State's DNA testing procedures that consumed certain samples because defendant was not prevented from cross-examining witnesses or presenting complete defense; [2]-In the prosecution for nine counts of first degree murder and other crimes involving a total of 32 victims and lasting seven and a half months, the trial court reasonably permitted the parties to make brief opening statements before trial on each of 13 chronological "chapters" corresponding to the dates of the offenses to orient jurors; [3]-No due process error resulted from the in-court identifications, even though police disseminated defendant's composite sketch and photo to media and those images were seen by witnesses.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

9 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Brown v. McClennen


No. CV-15-0042-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


239 Ariz. 521; 373 P.3d 538; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 117; 737 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



April 26, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ariz. v. Brown, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 5310 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the North Mesa Justice Court. No. JC2013-427663. Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Crane McClennen, Judge. No. LC2013-427663. Order of the Court of Appeals, Division One. Filed Dec. 30, 2014.
Brown v. McClennen, 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 271 (Ariz., Sept. 1, 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART, REMANDED IN PART. VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's consent to providing a blood sample was involuntary because by telling him that Arizona law required him to submit to and complete testing, an admonition that did not mirror the implied consent statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 5-395.03(A), the deputy invoked lawful authority and effectively proclaimed that defendant had no right to resist the search; [2]-The exclusionary rule applied because the inevitable discovery exception could not excuse the failure to secure a warrant in the first place; the sheriff's office would not have inevitably obtained defendant's blood sample by lawful, independent means.


OUTCOME: Reversed in part and remanded. Superior court judgment vacated.

 

10 of 1194 DOCUMENTS



State v. Valenzuela


No. CR-15-0222-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


239 Ariz. 299; 371 P.3d 627; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 116; 737 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 6



April 26, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Cochise County. The Honorable Karl D. Elledge, Judge. No. CR-201300076. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two. 237 Ariz. 307, 350 P.3d 811 (App. 2015) [***1] .
State v. Valenzuela, 237 Ariz. 307, 350 P.3d 811, 2015 Ariz. App. LEXIS 66 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The State failed to carry its burden to show that defendant freely and voluntarily consented to providing samples of his blood and breath because by advising him after he was arrested and detained that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1321(A) required him to submit to testing, the officer invoked lawful authority to compel consent; because nothing in the suppression hearing record dispelled the coercive implication of the officer's repeated admonition, the trial court erred by finding that defendant had voluntarily consented to the search and then denying the motion to suppress the test results on that basis; [2]-Because the officer did not deliberately, recklessly, or with gross negligence conduct the search, but instead acted with an objectively reasonable good-faith belief that the admonition was lawful, the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.


 

11 of 1194 DOCUMENTS



Watts v. Medicis Pharm. Corp.


No. CV-15-0065-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


239 Ariz. 19; 365 P.3d 944; 2016 Ariz. LEXIS 33; 730 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



January 21, 2016, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Lisa Daniel Flores, Judge. No. CV2012-008081. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 236 Ariz. 511, 342 P.3d 847 (App. 2015) [***1] .
Watts v. Medicis Pharm. Corp., 236 Ariz. 511, 342 P.3d 847, 2015 Ariz. App. LEXIS 12 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2015)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED. AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The superior court erred in dismissing the patient's product liability claim; if the manufacturer established that there was no genuine factual dispute that it provided complete, adequate warnings for the drug to the patient's prescribing physician and other health-care providers who were in a position to reduce the risks of harm, the learned intermediary doctrine (LID) applied and, as a matter of law, it satisfied its duty to warn and would be entitled to summary judgment; [2]-The LID was not displaced by the Arizona Uniform Contribution Among Tortfeasors Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2505; [3]-The patient alleged an actionable claim under the Arizona Consumer Fraud Act, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 44-1522(A) because it applied to prescription pharmaceuticals; she claimed that the manufacturer affirmatively misrepresented the drug and that the drug caused her drug-induced lupus.


OUTCOME: Judgment of court of appeals vacated in part and affirmed in part. Judgment of superior court reversed and remanded.


 

12 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Merrill v. Merrill


No. CV-15-0028-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


238 Ariz. 467; 362 P.3d 1034; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 362; 728 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 12



December 15, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Remanded by Merrill v. Merrill, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 3294 (U.S., May 22, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Paul J. McMurdie, Judge. No. DR1991-092542. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 1 CA-CV 13-0649. Filed Dec. 18, 2014. Amended Per Order Filed Jan. 7, 2015.
Merrill v. Merrill, 2014 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1520 (Dec. 18, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The appellate court erred by applying Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-318.01 to dismiss the former wife's petition because the statute could not apply to prevent the family court from fashioning an order to redress the reduction in military retirement pay (MRP) caused by the former husband's election to receive Combat-Related Special Compensation (CRSC) benefits since the wife's rights in her share of MRP vested before the effective date of the amendment to the statute; the statute could not apply to preclude indemnification when a retired veteran made a post-decree waiver of MRP to obtain CRSC benefits and the decree was entered before the statute's effective date.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and case remanded.

 

13 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Marriage of Howell


No. CV-15-0030-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


238 Ariz. 407; 361 P.3d 936; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 359; 727 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 25



December 2, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Howell v. Howell, 136 S. Ct. 1704, 194 L. Ed. 2d 765, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 2787 (U.S., Apr. 18, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari granted by Howell v. Howell, 137 S. Ct. 546, 196 L. Ed. 2d 441, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 7271 (U.S., Dec. 2, 2016)
Reversed by, Remanded by Howell v. Howell, 2017 U.S. LEXIS 2946 (U.S., May 15, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Danelle B. Liwski, Judge. No. D78235. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 2 CA-CV 2014-0112.
In re Marriage of Howell, 2014 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1561 (Dec. 18, 2014)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The family court properly determined that the former wife had a vested property right in fifty percent of the military retirement pay (MPR), and neither the former husband's election nor Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-318.01 could deprive her of this right because federal law did not preempt a family court's authority to order a retired veteran to indemnify an ex-spouse for a reduction in MRP caused by a post-decree waiver of MRP made to obtain disability benefits, and Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 25-318.01 could not be applied to prohibit the family court from entering an indemnification order in these circumstances if the ex-spouse's share of MRP vested as a property right before the statute's enactment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

14 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Havatone


No. CR-15-0387-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


241 Ariz. 506; 389 P.3d 1251; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 373; 760 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



October 27, 2015, Filed; March 9, 2017, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Mohave County. The Honorable Derek C. Carlisle, Judge Pro Tempore. No. CR201201535. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 1 CA-CR 14-0223.
State v. Havatone, 2015 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1298 (2015)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Mohave County, REVERSED AND REMANDED. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's U.S. Const. amend. IV rights were violated because the blood test under the unconscious clause, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1321(C), was taken pursuant to a blanket policy rather than the presence of case-specific exigent circumstances; the police department's practice of directing routine, warrantless, nonconsensual blood draws from DUI suspects sent outside the state for medical treatment was not objectively reasonable under Arizona law at the time of the draw; [2]-It was necessary to remand the case to determine whether Arizona or Nevada law applied; if Nevada law applied, the trial court was to determine whether the good-faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied.


OUTCOME: Judgment of court of appeals vacated; trial court's judgment reversed; case remanded.

 

15 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lynch


No. CR-12-0359-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


238 Ariz. 84; 357 P.3d 119; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 301; 721 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



September 10, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reversed by, Remanded by, Motion granted by Lynch v. Arizona, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 3487 (U.S., May 31, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Karen L. O'Connor, Judge. No. CR2001-092032.
State v. Lynch, 225 Ariz. 27, 234 P.3d 595, 2010 Ariz. LEXIS 25 (Ariz., 2010)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a capital murder case at a second sentencing trial, a prosecutor's argumentative comments during opening statement, aggressive cross-examination, and attacks on the defense theory (rather than on defendant or defense counsel) during closing did not deny defendant a fair trial; [2]-Because the defense had elicited testimony that defendant could be safely housed in prison, the State's cross-examination regarding escapes and the danger defendant posed due to his hepatitis C was relevant rebuttal under Ariz. R. Evid. 401(a) and Ariz. R. Evid. 611(b); [3]-Evidence supported a finding that the murder was especially cruel pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(6), because defendant and/or another tied defendant securely to a chair and slit his throat, but did not cut the spinal column so his nervous system remained intact so that he felt pain until he lost consciousness.


OUTCOME: Death sentence affirmed.

 

16 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Leteve


No. CR-12-0535-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


237 Ariz. 516; 354 P.3d 393; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 223; 719 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 11



August 12, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Leteve v. Ariz., 2016 U.S. LEXIS 799 (U.S., Jan. 19, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Karen L. O'Connor, Judge. No. CR2010-005965.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in admitting statements that defendant made to officers at his home before he was given Miranda warnings because the statements were admissible under the "public safety" exception to the Miranda rule; the officers reasonably asked questions to assess what had occurred, to determine injuries to those present, and to identify any remaining threats; [2]-Challenged other acts evidence was admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 404(b) to show defendant's intent or motive; the past difficulties between defendant and his wife were relevant to his intent and motive in killing their sons; [3]-While the trial court erred by instructing the jury that it could find the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(6) aggravator based on the parental relationship alone, the error was harmless due to the overwhelming evidence that the murders were senseless and the victims helpless.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Roseberry


No. CR-14-0277-PC


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


237 Ariz. 507; 353 P.3d 847; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 212; 718 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



July 27, 2015, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Roseberry v. Arizona, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 517 (U.S., Jan. 11, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On Review from the Superior Court in Yavapai County. The Honorable Celé Hancock, Judge. No. CR 20010177.
State v. Roseberry, 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 158 (Ariz., May 26, 2015)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant was not entitled to a new penalty phase hearing based on his claim that his appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to timely raise the issue of an unconstitutional jury instruction because he was not prejudiced by the alleged deficiency in counsel's representation; any error in the jury instruction was cured when the court considered all mitigation evidence in its independent review of the entire record pursuant to Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-755 and found it insufficient to call for leniency.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

18 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Carlson


No. CR-12-0464-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


237 Ariz. 381; 351 P.3d 1079; 2015 Ariz. LEXIS 197; 715 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



June 18, 2015, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Richard D. Nichols, Judge. No. CR20093544-001.
State v. Carlson, 228 Ariz. 343, 266 P.3d 369, 2011 Ariz. App. LEXIS 200 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2011)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in admitting defendant's incriminating statements to a television reporter as evidence of the two kidnapping counts because, under the corpus delicti rule, the State met its burden for both charges; blood and DNA evidence linked to the victims was found in his car; [2]-The exclusion of an expert's testimony did not violate defendant's right to present a defense; allowing the expert to testify that defendant said he falsely confessed would have put defendant's statements before the jury cloaked with the implication that the expert believed those statements and relied on them, while shielding defendant from the rigors of cross-examination; [3]-The use of defendant's kidnapping convictions as both aggravating factors under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(2) and predicate felonies for felony murder did not violate the federal or Arizona constitutions.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

19 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Biggs v. Cooper


No. CV-14-0132-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


236 Ariz. 415; 341 P.3d 457; 2014 Ariz. LEXIS 221; 703 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



December 31, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, On remand at Biggs v. Betlach, 2017 Ariz. App. LEXIS 50 (Ariz. Ct. App., Mar. 16, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Katherine M. Cooper, Judge. No. CV2013-011699. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 234 Ariz. 515, 323 P.3d 1166 (2014) [***1] .
Biggs v. Cooper, 234 Ariz. 515, 323 P.3d 1166, 2014 Ariz. App. LEXIS 68 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2014)



DISPOSITION: REVERSED IN PART; REMANDED. AFFIRMED IN PART; VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A group of legislators who voted against a house bill had standing to challenge whether it was passed in a constitutional manner; [2]-Because the votes of the bloc of the legislators here would have sufficed to defeat the house bill if a supermajority was required for enactment under Ariz. Const. art. 9, § 22(A), the group alleged that its members' votes were effectively nullified; [3]-Because there had been no determination on the merits, an award of attorneys' fees was denied without prejudice to the legislators' seeking an award from the superior court if they ultimately prevailed in the lawsuit.


OUTCOME: Reversed in part, affirmed in part, vacated in part, and remanded.

 

20 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Gallardo v. State


No. CV-14-0208-PR/A


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


236 Ariz. 84; 336 P.3d 717; 2014 Ariz. LEXIS 181



October 30, 2014, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Randall H. Warner, Judge. No. CV2013-017137. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One 691 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 36     Ariz.    , 335 P.3d 523, 2014 Ariz. App. LEXIS 127 (2014) WL 3671571. [***1] 
Gallardo v. State, 335 P.3d 523, 2014 Ariz. App. LEXIS 127 (Ariz. Ct. App., July 23, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-1441(I) did not violate the special laws provision of Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 19, because reasons such as facilitating community college district governance and increasing representation and perhaps diversity on governing boards rationally related to legitimate governmental interests common to the whole state, the class was legitimate and reasonably included (at present) the lone member of the affected class, and the class was facially and functionally elastic.


OUTCOME: Opinion of the court of appeals vacated and judgment of the superior court affirmed.

 

21 of 1194 DOCUMENTS



State ex rel. Montgomery v. Harris


No. CV-13-0056-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


237 Ariz. 98; 346 P.3d 984; 2014 Ariz. LEXIS 93



April 22, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reported at State ex rel. Montgomery v. Harris, 234 Ariz. 343, 2014 Ariz. LEXIS 229 (Ariz., 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Arcadia Biltmore Justice Court. The Honorable David Fletcher, Judge Pro Tempore. No. TR 2011-100433. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Myra Harris, Commissioner. No. LC 2011-100433-001. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One. 232 Ariz. 76, 301 P.3d 580 (2013) [***1] .
State ex rel. Montgomery v. Harris, 322 P.3d 160, 2014 Ariz. LEXIS 228 (Ariz., 2014)
State ex rel. Montgomery v. Harris, 232 Ariz. 76, 301 P.3d 580, 2013 Ariz. App. LEXIS 25 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2013)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Arcadia Biltmore Justice Court, AFFIRMED. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Dismissal of the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3) charge was proper, since Carboxy-Tetrahydrocannabinol, the only metabolite found in defendant's blood, did not cause impairment, when the "metabolite" reference in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3) was limited to any of a proscribed substance's metabolites that were capable of causing impairment, and drivers could not be convicted of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 28-1381(A)(3) based merely on the presence of a non-impairing metabolite that could reflect the prior usage of marijuana.


OUTCOME: The trial court's dismissal of the charge affirmed.

State v. Boyston


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0052-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 539; 298 P.3d 887; 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 104



April 15, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Boyston v. Arizona, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 7025 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court. No. CR2004-007442-001. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable John R. Ditsworth, Judge. The Honorable Joseph C. Welty, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) of three first degree murders and one count each of attempted first and second degree murder. He was sentenced to death for the murders and to prison terms on the attempt convictions. He appealed his convictions and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant said an Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-753(K)(2) mental retardation expert lacked requisite experience. The supreme court disagreed because (1) he had at least five years' experience, and (2) the statute imposed no other requirements. It was no error to admit his testimony because nothing showed he did not use currently accepted procedures. IQ scores created no mental retardation presumption because some evidence questioned the scores. Jurors were not excluded for death penalty views because (1) a juror was highly conflicted about the death penalty, and (2) another was excused for credibility issues. Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-503 barred voluntary intoxication evidence when considering premeditation because, while not a "culpable" mental state under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-105(10), premeditation was part of the crime's mens rea element, under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1105(A)(1). It was not error not to instruct on manslaughter because the jury rejected second degree murder. Sufficient evidence supported the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(8) and (F)(6) aggravators because (1) the murders were temporally and spatially related, and (2) a jury could find they were motivationally related.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were affirmed.

State v. Rose


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0362-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 500; 297 P.3d 906; 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 102

Baker v. Univ. Physicians Healthcare


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-12-0102-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 379; 296 P.3d 42; 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 59; 656 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 17



March 12, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division Two No. 2 CA-CV 11-0080. Pima County Superior Court No. C20097222. Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Richard E. Gordon, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, 228 Ariz. 587, 269 P.3d 1211 (2011).
Baker v. Univ. Physicians Healthcare, 228 Ariz. 587, 269 P.3d 1211, 2012 Ariz. App. LEXIS 24 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2012)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, VACATED AND REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged a decision from the Pima County Superior Court, Arizona, which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee employer in a wrongful death case based on medical malpractice. Further review was granted after the Arizona Court of Appeals, Division Two, partially reversed the trial court's decision and remanded the case.


OVERVIEW: After a minor patient died, and her father filed a wrongful-death action alleging medical malpractice of a treating physician, who was certified in pediatrics and pediatric hematology-oncology. The trial court found that an expert certified in internal medicine, hematology, and medical oncology was not qualified under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2604. Summary judgment was entered against the father, but the court of appeals partially reversed the trial court's decision. After a remand was ordered, the supreme court granted review. In partially vacating the court of appeals' opinion, the supreme court determined that "specialty" for purposes of § 12-2604 was construed as referring to a limited area of medicine in which a physician could have become board certified. However, the courts of appeals' determination that "specialty" did not include subspecialities was rejected. Section 12-2604 required a testifying expert to be board certified in the same speciality as the treating physician because she was practicing within her specialty of pediatric hematology-oncology. The father's constitutional arguments relating to § 12-2604 were rejected.


OUTCOME: The opinion of the court of appeals was vacated, except insofar as it vacated the trial court's judgment and directed the trial court on remand to allow an opportunity to identify an expert with the qualifications required by Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 12-2604. The case was remanded to the trial court for proceedings consistent with this opinion.

State v. Ovante


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0085-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 180; 291 P.3d 974; 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 22; 652 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



January 11, 2013, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Ovante v. Arizona, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 5971 (U.S., Oct. 7, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2008-144114-001 DT. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Warren J. Granville, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED AS AMENDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty to two counts of first degree murder under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1105(A)(1) (2008) and aggravated assault. He admitted aggravating circumstances. The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, entered sentences of life with a possibility of parole after 25 years for the first murder count, death for the second murder, and 6 years in prison for aggravated assault. He received an automatic appeal of the death sentence.


OVERVIEW: In a death penalty case, the Supreme Court of Arizona reviewed the validity of defendant's plea to two counts of first degree murder before it reviewed the capital sentence. The trial court was free to accept the guilty plea if the record established premeditation. The circumstantial evidence and defendant's statements supported a finding that he reflected on the killings before pulling the trigger. The record did not show that the State sought the death penalty for a discriminatory or improper reason. The prosecutor's comments did not create fundamental error. At the penalty phase, the State was allowed to present evidence of the circumstances of his crimes. The jury instructions were accurate and not misleading. Given the aggravating circumstances, the jury's imposition of the death sentence was not an abuse of discretion under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-756(A).


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed as amended. The minute entry was corrected to delete statements indicating defendant's sentences would run concurrently. Instead, all sentences were to run consecutively.

Rumery v. Baier


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-11-0358-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 275; 294 P.3d 113; 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 2; 651 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



January 9, 2013, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division One No. 1 CA-CV 10-0807. Maricopa County Superior Court No. CV2010-012871. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Gary E. Donahoe, Judge (Ret.). Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 228 Ariz. 463, 268 P.3d 1120 (2011).
Rumery v. Baier, 228 Ariz. 463, 268 P.3d 1120, 2011 Ariz. App. LEXIS 190 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2011)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Review was granted after the Arizona Court of Appeals Division One, affirmed a trial court's decision to grant summary judgment in favor of appellee objectors and its determination that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 37-527 violated Ariz. Const. art. 10, § 7 and the New Mexico-Arizona Enabling Act.


OVERVIEW: It was alleged that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 37-527 (Supp. 2012), which diverted up to 10 percent of certain trust land proceeds to a management fund, violated Ariz. Const. art. 10, § 7(A). The trial court enjoined appellant Arizona State Land Commissioner from designating state trust land proceeds for deposit into the management fund. The court of appeals affirmed, and the supreme court granted review. On review, the supreme court noted that the use of trust lands or their proceeds was not allowed if it involved ways that there not expressly authorized, even if it would have benefitted the trust. The supreme court applied Ariz. Const. art. 10, § 7 according to its terms, and it declined to infer unstated exceptions to its restrictions on the use of state trust land proceeds. The constitutional language here controlled over the common law of trusts. The Arizona Constitution's silence on the payment of the costs of trust management and the fact that such expenditures might have benefitted the trusts were not sufficient grounds for reading exceptions into the Arizona Constitution or the Enabling Act.


OUTCOME: The trial court's entry of summary judgment was affirmed, and the decision from the court of appeals was vacated. An award of attorney's fees was entered against the Commissioner.

 

38 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gomez


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0358-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


231 Ariz. 219; 293 P.3d 495; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 259



December 7, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gomez v. Arizona, 133 S. Ct. 2339, 185 L. Ed. 2d 1070, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 3833 (U.S., May 13, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2000-090114. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Roland J. Steinle, Judge.
State v. Gomez, 211 Ariz. 494, 123 P.3d 1131, 2005 Ariz. LEXIS 129 (Ariz., 2005)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, convicted defendant of first degree murder, kidnapping, and sexual assault. Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that, after the case was remanded for resentencing, the trial court erred by revoking his pro per status and appointing counsel to represent him. The supreme court noted that a trial court may revoke pro per status for serious violations of court orders and rules even if the conduct occurred outside a courtroom proceeding. Defendant demonstrated that he could not comply with court deadlines and the disclosure rules. A trial judge was not required to hold an evidentiary hearing on a motion for change of counsel if the motion failed to allege specific facts suggesting an irreconcilable conflict or a complete breakdown in communication, or if there was no indication that a hearing would elicit additional facts beyond those already before the court. The record established beyond a reasonable doubt that the victim's murder was especially cruel. The State proved that defendant knew or should have known that the victim was suffering physically and mentally. The mitigating circumstances were not substantial. The State's cross-appeal was moot because the supreme court affirmed defendant's death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Joseph


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0138-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 296; 283 P.3d 27; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 174; 641 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 35



August 17, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Joseph v. Ariz., 133 S. Ct. 936, 184 L. Ed. 2d 733, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 786 (U.S., Jan. 14, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2005-014235-001. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Arthur T. Anderson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, convicted defendant of felony murder and other crimes. He was sentenced to death for the murder and to prison terms for the other convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the trial court violated his U.S. Const. amend. VI right to confront the doctor who prepared the autopsy report when, over his objection, it allowed the State's medical expert to testify based on the report. The supreme court noted that the court did not admit the autopsy report into evidence and the State presented testimony by a witness subject to cross-examination. The expert testified to opinions he formed after reviewing facts and photographs contained in the report. The trial court did not err in permitting the expert to testify about the basis for his conclusions regarding the victim's injuries and cause of death. There was sufficient evidence to support the imposition of the death penalty. Defendant did not dispute that he shot and killed the victim during the commission of a felony. Defendant's waiver of his right to present mitigation was voluntary, knowing, and informed, Ariz. R. Crim. P. 15.2(h). The jury did not abuse its discretion in concluding that the mitigating circumstances were not sufficiently substantial to call for leniency.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Martinez


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0177-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 208; 282 P.3d 409; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 172; 641 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 27



August 17, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Martinez v. Ariz., 133 S. Ct. 764, 184 L. Ed. 2d 505, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 9310 (U.S., Dec. 3, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County, Superior Court No. CR2006-007790-001 DT. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Rosa Mroz, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona), which convicted him of first-degree burglary, four counts of aggravated assault, four counts of kidnapping, theft, and first-degree murder, and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of burglary, aggravated assault, kidnapping, theft, and murder. After a mistrial in the penalty phase, a second jury determined that he should be sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found that the trial court did not err in allowing the State to use 19 prior serious felony convictions to prove the aggravator in Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(2). Each conviction was probative in the penalty phase to show his character and propensities and to strengthen the weight of the aggravator. While the prosecutor's courtroom conduct of eye-rolling and facial expressions was inappropriate, it was confirmed only twice by the trial judge, who did not think it amounted to such pervasive misconduct as to bar retrial of the penalty phase. The trial court did not err under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-752(G) in allowing the State to present evidence during the penalty phase that defendant claimed to have been at a strip club at the time of the murder. Because defendant claimed he had a low IQ and brain damage, evidence that he claimed to have been at a club when the murder occurred showed he was able to fabricate an alibi.


OUTCOME: The convictions and sentence were affirmed.

Escamilla v. Cuello


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-12-0039-AP/EL


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 202; 282 P.3d 403; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 173; 641 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 24



August 17, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Yuma County Superior Court No. CV201101582. Appeal from the Superior Court in Yuma County. The Honorable John Neff Nelson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Yuma County, Arizona, disqualified appellant candidate under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-201(C) (2001) from appearing on the ballot as a candidate for the city council. The candidate appealed.


OVERVIEW: The candidate argued that the superior court erred in issuing its order twenty-nine days after appellee elector filed the complaint. The supreme court noted that the trial court's processing of the case left sufficient time for expedited appellate review before the ballot printing deadline. Because the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 16-351(A) deadline for decision was not jurisdictional and the candidate did not show prejudice, there was no error. The supreme court noted that the most plausible and harmonious reading of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 38-201(C) was that it required a sufficient level of proficiency of the English language to conduct the duties of the office without the aid of an interpreter. The testimony supported the trial court's conclusions that the candidate failed to comprehend the questions posed to her. Her testimony showed minimal English language comprehension. The candidate's inability to comprehend English was clear and the trial court properly disqualified her. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting the expert's testimony. The candidate was not forever barred from running for office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Hardy


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0224-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 281; 283 P.3d 12; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 171; 641 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 38



August 16, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Hardy v. Ariz., 133 S. Ct. 935, 184 L. Ed. 2d 732, 2013 U.S. LEXIS 853 (U.S., Jan. 14, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2005-127282-001 SE. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Michael W. Kemp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged a decision from the Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, which convicted him of first degree burglary, kidnapping, and two counts of first degree murder and imposed the death sentence on the murder counts.


OVERVIEW: Appellant's wife was staying with a friend. Finally, the jury did not abuse its discretion in finding that the mitigation evidence was insufficient to warrant leniency.

State v. Nordstrom


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0266-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA

State v. Hausner


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0077-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 60; 280 P.3d 604; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 160



July 10, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court Nos. CR2006-012721-001 DT, CR2006-048493-002 DT, CR2007-006031-001 DT, CR2008-006364-001 DT, CR2008-007313-002 DT. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Roland J. Steinle, Judge.
State v. Hausner, 2011 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 586 (Feb. 22, 2011)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED IN PART; REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of six murders and 74 noncapital offenses in the Superior Court in Maricopa County (Arizona). He was sentenced to, inter alia, death for each of the murder convictions. Defendant challenged the convictions and sentences.


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not commit reversible error in granting the State's motion to strike two potential jurors where one juror was not among the final pool of jurors and the other had a desire not to serve and had made conflicting statements regarding the death penalty. The trial court did not err in failing to suppress recorded conversations obtained by wiretap in his apartment where the wiretaps had been authorized by the county attorney in order to prevent another random shooting, thus establishing an immediate danger of death or serious physical injury as required by Ariz. Evidence at the suppression hearing also established that conventional wiretaps could not have been obtained through due diligence. The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motions to sever. However, the evidence was insufficient to sustain one conviction for animal cruelty where a jury could not have reasonably concluded from the circumstances that defendant had shot a horse.


OUTCOME: The conviction as to one animal cruelty count was reversed, but the remaining convictions and sentences were affirmed.

Mario W. v. Kaipio


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-11-0344-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


230 Ariz. 122; 281 P.3d 476; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 153



June 27, 2012, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division One Nos. 1 CA-SA 11-0016, 1 CA-SA 11-0020, 1 CA-SA 11-0025, 1 CA-SA 11-0031, 1 CA-SA 11-0032, 1 CA-SA 11-0042, 1 CA-SA 11-0043 (Consolidated). Maricopa County Superior Court Nos. JV-181946, JV-181821, JV-555266, JV-555329, JV-555361, JV-555390, JV-555429. Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Thomas A. Kaipio, Judge Pro Tem. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 228 Ariz. 207, 265 P.3d 389 (App. 2011).
Mario W. v. Kaipio, 228 Ariz. 207, 265 P.3d 389, 2011 Ariz. App. LEXIS 182 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2011)



DISPOSITION: Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Arizona Court of Appeals held that requiring the submission of DNA samples from five juveniles for whom a probable cause determination had been made did not violate the Fourth Amendment, U.S. Const. amend. IV. The State and two juveniles petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the issue was whether the State, consistent with the Fourth Amendment, could compel the juveniles to submit to DNA extraction and profiling as a condition of release? The supreme court determined that even if extracting the cell sample did not intrude on privacy to the same extent as a search of the home or the drawing of blood, it remained a search or seizure under the Fourth Amendment. Under the totality of the circumstances test, the issue was whether, and to what degree, that intrusion served important governmental interests. The State had an important interest in locating an absconding juvenile and ascertaining that the person located was the one previously charged. If the State could not obtain a DNA sample from a juvenile before release, it may never have another opportunity to do so. The physical extraction of the DNA was constitutional as to all of the juveniles. No state interest sufficiently justified the serious intrusion on the privacy interests of the juveniles occasioned by the extraction of the DNA profile from the buccal swab before adjudication or failure to appear.


OUTCOME: The opinion of the court of appeals was vacated and the cases remanded to the superior court for further proceedings.

Ariz. Indep. Redistricting Comm'n v. Brewer


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-11-0313-SA


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


229 Ariz. 347; 275 P.3d 1267; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 97; 632 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 32



April 20, 2012, Decided


DISPOSITION:  [***1] JURISDICTION ACCEPTED; RELIEF GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Arizona Independent Redistricting Committee (IRC) sought special action relief to challenge the removal of intervenor chairperson from the IRC by respondent Arizona Governor.


OVERVIEW: A special action was filed seeking to challenge the Governor's removal of a chairperson from the IRC under Ariz. Const. art. 4, pt. 2, § 1(10). The IRC contended that the Governor had exceeded her limited removal authority and that the Governor and respondent Senate had violated separation-of-powers principals. In granting relief, the supreme court determined that it had original subject matter jurisdiction in this case. It exercised its discretion to accept special action jurisdiction because the legal issues raised required prompt resolution and were of first impression and statewide importance. Next, the chairperson had standing because she was displaced from office, and there was no need to determine if the IRC had standing. Further, appellate review of whether the Governor complied with the constitutional legal standards in removing the chairperson was not barred by the political question doctrine. However, the case failed on the merits because neither of the grounds advanced by the Governor amounted to a removal with legal cause.


OUTCOME: The relief sought was granted, and reinstatement was ordered.

State v. Nelson


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0343-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


229 Ariz. 180; 273 P.3d 632; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 92



April 12, 2012, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Nelson v. Ariz., 184 L. Ed. 2d 63, 2012 U.S. LEXIS 6705 (U.S., Oct. 1, 2012)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Mohave County Superior Court No. CR20060904. Appeal from the Superior Court in Mohave County. The Honorable Richard Weiss, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Mohave County, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Mohave County Superior Court (Arizona) of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that his conviction should be vacated because the State's evidence showed only passage of time but not the actual reflection required for premeditation under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-1101(1). The supreme court disagreed. Defendant was caring for his fourteen-year old niece, the victim. On the day of the murder, defendant left the motel room and walked to a store where he purchased a rubber mallet. Defendant returned to the motel and hit the victim in the head with the mallet and covered her with a blanket on the bed. Police officers found a bloody black sock containing a rubber mallet hidden under the bed. They also found men's jeans with blood on them. The sock and jeans contained DNA from both the victim and defendant. Police also found the victim's pants "turned inside out, with the panties still within them and the socks within the legs of the pants" as if "somebody had pulled them off." The medical examiner also found defendant's semen on the victim's body. Therefore, the evidence was sufficient to show premeditation and sustain defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Motion granted by Cota v. Ryan, 2017 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 25437 (D. Ariz., Feb. 23, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court Nos. CR2004-006577-001 DT, CR2004-005648-001 DT (CONSOLIDATED). Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Michael D. Jones, Judge.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, convicted defendant of two counts of first degree murder, two counts of armed robbery, one count of possession of narcotics, and one count of unlawful flight. Nunez v. Prof'l Transit Mgmt. of Tucson, Inc.


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-11-0186-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


229 Ariz. 117; 271 P.3d 1104; 2012 Ariz. LEXIS 123



February 23, 2012, Decided 
February 23, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division Two No. 2 CA-CV 10-0201. Pima County Superior Court No. C20090652. Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Stephen C. Villarreal, Judge. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two.
Nunez v. Prof'l Transit Mgmt. of Tucson, Inc., 2011 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 683 (2011)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, VACATED AND REMANDED. Memorandum Decision of the Court of Appeals, Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a negligence action stemming from an injury to plaintiff passenger during a bus ride, defendants, the bus company and one of its bus drivers, appealed a judgment of the Pima County Superior Court (Arizona) in favor of the passenger, arguing that the trial court erred in instructing the jury that they had a duty to exercise the highest degree of care practicable under the circumstances rather than only the duty to exercise reasonable care.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff passenger was wheelchair bound. After she boarded a bus, the bus driver secured her wheelchair to the bus floor. As the bus resumed its travel, a car stopped abruptly in front of it, causing the driver to brake sharply. The passenger was thrown from her wheelchair and sustained injury. She sued the bus company and driver. At trial, defendants requested that the trial court instruct the jury that the standard of care required of them was that of reasonable care; the trial court rejected the request and instructed the jury that a common carrier had the duty to exercise the highest decree of care practicable under the circumstances. On review of the judgment in favor of the passenger, the court held that a heightened standard of care was no longer applicable to common carriers. Rather, the appropriate standard of care in negligence actions by passengers against common carrier was the objective and reasonable person standard in traditional negligence law. If the carrier acted with reasonable care in light of all the circumstances, it discharged its duty to its passengers.


OUTCOME: The judgment in favor of the passenger was reversed, and the case was remanded for a new trial.

State v. Lehr


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0095-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


227 Ariz. 140; 254 P.3d 379; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 37



July 13, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Lehr v. Ariz., 132 S. Ct. 403, 181 L. Ed. 2d 263, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 7325 (U.S., Oct. 11, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR1992-005731. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Andrew G. Klein, Judge.
State v. Lehr, 205 Ariz. 107, 67 P.3d 703, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 60 (Ariz., 2003)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) that convicted him of murdering two women and imposed death sentences, arguing that the trial court erred in permitting the State to introduce other acts evidence under Ariz. R. Evid. 404(c)(1) and erred in failing to give a limiting instruction to the jury regarding the use of such other acts evidence.


OVERVIEW: Over the course of a year, defendant abducted and sexually assaulted 10 women and brutally murdered three of them. On review, the court held that the trial court did not err in admitting other acts evidence under Ariz. R. Evid. 404(c)(1) because evidence of the other acts provided a reasonable basis to infer that defendant had a character trait that gave rise to an aberrant sexual propensity for violent and sexual acts against non-consenting females and because the evidence established modus operandi and identity in that the attacks were strikingly similar in the way defendant lured the victims and transported them to the area where he then assaulted them, how he assaulted them, where he assaulted them, and how he left them. Further, although the trial court erred in failing to specify in its limiting instruction the purposes for which the other acts evidence was being admitted, the failure was harmless because the purposes for which the evidence was admitted were apparent from the record. In closing arguments, the State urged the jury to consider the evidence only for the purposes for which it had been offered: to show modus operandi, identity, and an aberrant sexual propensity.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence was affirmed.

State v. Prince

May 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Prince v. Arizona, 132 S. Ct. 582, 181 L. Ed. 2d 428, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 8258 (U.S., 2011)
Post-conviction relief denied at, Petition granted by State v. Prince, 2013 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 499 (2013)
Subsequent appeal at, Motion to strike denied by, As moot In re State, 2013 Ariz. App. Unpub. LEXIS 1199 (2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court. No. CR1998-004885. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Sally Schneider Duncan, Judge.
State v. Prince, 206 Ariz. 24, 75 P.3d 114, 2003 Ariz. LEXIS 110 (Ariz., 2003)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona) convicting him of first-degree murder and attempted first-degree murder, and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court held that Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-752(K) was not void for vagueness because the statutes governing the second penalty phase, Ariz. Rev. Stat. §§ 13-752(G), 13-751(G), provided sufficient guidance for the admissibility of evidence of the aggravating factors previously found by the aggravation-phase jury. The trifurcated jury proceedings did not violate defendant's constitutional rights because he did not point to any relevant evidence that was excluded from the second penalty jury's consideration because of the trifurcated proceeding, as substantially the same evidence was introduced at the second sentencing trial as at the first. The trial court did not err by striking a juror under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 21-201(3) because he was a convicted felon who did not aver that his civil rights had been restored. Even if reading the transcript of the State's gun expert's guilt-phase testimony into evidence during the aggravation phase violated defendant's Confrontation Clause rights, he failed to show that he was prejudiced, as the testimony was irrelevant to the Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(9) aggravating factor.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

State v. Dixon


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-08-0025-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 545; 250 P.3d 1174; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 23



May 6, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Dixon v. Arizona, 132 S. Ct. 456, 181 L. Ed. 2d 297, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 7463 (U.S., 2011)
Writ of habeas corpus denied, Motion denied by, Stay vacated by, Certificate of appealability granted, in part Dixon v. Ryan, 2016 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 33999 (D. Ariz., Mar. 16, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court. No. CR2002-019595. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Andrew G. Klein, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, that convicted him of first-degree murder and sentenced him to death, arguing that the trial court erred in excluding the victim's diary and that the evidence failed to support the especially cruel under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(6)


OVERVIEW: In defendant's murder trial stemming from the rape and murder of a young woman, the trial court did not err in excluding an entry from the victim's diary in which she stated that she had been sexually assaulted while in Europe and would fight back if ever assaulted again. The court rejected defedant's argument that the evidence was admissible under Ariz. R. Evid. 803(3) to show that his sexual contact with the victim was consensual, as the victim likely would have forcibly resisted an assault, because the alleged statements had minimal probative value. The victim's state of mind years before the murder hardly established that she surely would have or could have used a knife or other weapon to prevent defendant's attack. The court further found that the murder was especially cruel under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(6) because the victim consciously suffered physical pain or mental anguish during at least some portion of the crime and defendant knew or should have known that she would suffer. The victim surely must have suffered mental anguish while being raped, hit, and strangled, and defendant should have known that the victim would suffer such anguish.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and death sentence were affirmed.

 

56 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Morehart v. Barton


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-10-0327-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 510; 250 P.3d 1139; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 22



April 29, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Subsequent appeal at, Sub nomine at State v. Miller, 2013 Ariz. LEXIS 283 (Ariz., Dec. 27, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division One No. 1 CA-SA 10-0126. Maricopa County Superior Court Nos. CR2005-140129, CR2006-112056. Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Janet E. Barton, Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 225 Ariz. 269, 236 P.3d 1216 (App. 2010).
Morehart v. Barton, 225 Ariz. 269, 236 P.3d 1216, 2010 Ariz. App. LEXIS 131 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Special Action from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Maricopa County Superior Court, Arizona, granted defendant's request for an ex parte hearing related to the defense investigation into mitigation matters. Petitioner family members (victims) sought special action in the Arizona Court of Appeals, which vacated the trial court's order. The court of appeals found that defendant's constitutional rights would not be jeopardized. Defendant petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court had to determine whether the victims were entitled under Arizona law to attend an ex parte hearing concerning defendant's pretrial mitigation discovery. The supreme court noted that the issue was whether exclusion of the victims would violate their rights "to be present at" a criminal proceeding where the defendant had the right to be present, Ariz. Const. art. 2, § 2.1(A)(3). The contemplated hearing was not one where the defendant had the right to be present as the hearing would concern purely procedural matters that did not implicate defendant's right to confront witnesses and evidence against him. The victims were not entitled to attend the contemplated ex part hearing because defendant did not have the right to be present.


OUTCOME: The judgment was vacated and remanded to the court of appeals for further proceedings.

 

57 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


Gutierrez v. Indus. Comm'n


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-10-0285-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 395; 249 P.3d 1095; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 21; 606 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 45



April 21, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division One No. 1 CA-IC 09-0040. ICA Claim No. 20071-150489. Carrier Claim No. 0712694. Special Action from the Industrial Commission of Arizona. The Honorable Stephen W. Pogson, Administrative Law Judge. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 226 Ariz. 1, 243 P.3d 604 (App. 2010).
Gutierrez v. Indus. Comm'n, 226 Ariz. 1, 243 P.3d 604, 2010 Ariz. App. LEXIS 217 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Special Action from the Industrial Commission of Arizona, AFFIRMED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a workers' compensation claimant, sought review of a decision entered by the Court of Appeals, Division One (Arizona), which affirmed a decision by respondent, the Industrial Commission of Arizona (ICA), that the claimant did not suffer a permanent impairment as a result of work-related injury.


OVERVIEW: Respondent insurance carrier determined that the claimant was not permanently impaired. The claimant's treating physician, using the Fifth Edition of the American Medical Association Guides to the Evaluation of Permanent Impairment (AMA Guides), testified at an ICA hearing that the claimant had suffered a 5% permanent impairment based on a resolved lumbar radiculopathy; the carrier's expert testified that the claimant had no ratable permanent impairment based on the Sixth Edition of the AMA Guides. The issue raised was the meaning of the "most recent edition" of the AMA Guides in Ariz. Admin. Code R20-5-113(B). On appeal, the court affirmed. To give the regulation a fair and sensible meaning, the court held that it referred to the standards in the edition of the AMA Guides most recently published before the claimant's impairment was rated. Thus, a doctor would consider the latest medical developments when determining impairment. The regulation did not improperly delegate the power of the ICA under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 23-921(B) (1995) to the AMA to set the standards physicians had to use to rate impairment because the use of the AMA Guides in impairment rating was discretionary.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decisions of the court of appeals and the ICA.

State v. Delahanty


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0133-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 502; 250 P.3d 1131; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 20; 605 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



April 8, 2011, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Delahanty v. Ariz., 2011 U.S. LEXIS 6343 (U.S., Oct. 3, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2005-114414. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Warren J. Granville, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Maricopa County Superior Court (Arizona), which convicted him of first-degree murder, attempted arson, conspiracy to commit first-degree murder, and solicitation to commit first-degree murder. He was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred under Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-754(A) in not ordering a competency pre-screening of defendant. However, defendant could not establish fundamental error. The record was replete with evidence that he understood the proceedings against him and was able to assist in his own defense. Further, the trial court did not err in declining requested defense instructions because no rational jury could have found that defendant committed a lesser-included offense. He shot a police officer three times at close range in the face and neck during a routine traffic stop, actions almost certain to bring about death. The officer was in full uniform and driving a marked police cruiser with its lights engaged. Finally, the trial court did not err in finding aggravated circumstances. Ample evidence supported the findings that defendant had been convicted of serious offenses, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(2), and that he knew or should have known that the victim was an on-duty police officer, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(10).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

State v. Montes


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-10-0017-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 194; 245 P.3d 879; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 7; 600 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 4



January 26, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division Two No. 2 CA-CR 08-0148. Pima County Superior Court No. CR20054089. Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County. The Honorable Howard L. Fell, Judge Pro Tem. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Division Two, 223 Ariz. 337, 223 P.3d 681 (App. 2009).
State v. Montes, 223 Ariz. 337, 223 P.3d 681, 2009 Ariz. App. LEXIS 784 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2009)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Pima County, REVERSED AND REMANDED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals Division Two, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of second-degree murder and two counts of aggravated assault. The Court of Appeals of Arizona affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences, and denied his motion for reconsideration. The state supreme court granted defendant's petition for review.


OVERVIEW: In 2006, SB 1145, 2006 Ariz. Sess. Laws, ch. 199, amended Arizona's self-defense statute, Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-205(A) (2003), to require the state to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that a defendant did not act with justification if he presented some evidence of justification. In 2008, defendant was tried for first-degree murder, and claimed he acted in self defense. The jury was instructed that defendant had to prove self-defense by a preponderance of the evidence. In 2009, the legislature enacted SB 1449, providing that SB 1145 applied retroactively. The Supreme Court of Arizona held that SB 1449 was a valid exercise of legislative authority and did not violate the separation of powers doctrine in Ariz. Const. art. 3. SB 1449 did not disturb victims' rights in the finality of a defendant's conviction. Section 2 of SB 1449 was severable from and not fatal to SB 1449's operative provision in section 1.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions and sentences were reversed, the court of appeals' opinion was vacated, and the case was remanded to the superior court for further proceedings.

 

60 of 1194 DOCUMENTS


In re Nickolas S.


Arizona Supreme Court No. CV-10-0092-PR


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


226 Ariz. 182; 245 P.3d 446; 2011 Ariz. LEXIS 1; 599 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 26



January 10, 2011, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Court of Appeals Division One No. 1 CA-JV 09-0147. Maricopa County Superior Court No. JV173845. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Joan M. Sinclair, Commissioner. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, 224 Ariz. 52, 226 P.3d 1038 (2010).
In re Nickolas S., 224 Ariz. 52, 226 P.3d 1038, 2010 Ariz. App. LEXIS 29 (Ariz. Ct. App., 2010)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, VACATED. Opinion of the Court of Appeals, Division One, VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, adjudicated defendant, a juvenile, delinquent for violating Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 15-507 (2009). The Arizona Court of Appeals held that when pure speech is involved, the statute applied only to "fighting words." Defendant petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the court of appeals misapplied the fighting words doctrine by focusing on the theoretical reaction of a hypothetical reasonable person instead of the likely reaction of the teacher addressed by the speech. The supreme court noted that for purposes of the fighting words doctrine, the inquiry is not whether a reasonable person "might" react violently, but instead whether someone in the circumstances of the addressee would likely react violently in the context in which the words were spoken. Considering the circumstances in which defendant uttered his words, his insults would not likely have provoked an ordinary teacher to exchange fisticuffs with the student or otherwise react violently. Defendant's conduct, in vulgarly insulting the teacher, although reprehensible, was properly punished through school discipline or possibly prosecution under other statutes rather than by characterizing it as fighting words likely to provoke a violent reaction by his teacher.


OUTCOME: The decision of the court of appeals was reversed insofar as it affirmed the adjudication of delinquency for the second incident; the opinion of the court of appeals was vacated and the juvenile court's order of adjudication was vacated as to both counts.

State v. Gallardo


Arizona Supreme Court No. CR-09-0171-AP


SUPREME COURT OF ARIZONA


225 Ariz. 560; 242 P.3d 159; 2010 Ariz. LEXIS 48; 596 Ariz. Adv. Rep. 7



November 30, 2010, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Gallardo v. Arizona, 179 L. Ed. 2d 665, 2011 U.S. LEXIS 2465 (U.S., Mar. 28, 2011)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
Maricopa County Superior Court No. CR2006-175408. Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County. The Honorable Sally Schneider Duncan, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Appeal from the Superior Court in Maricopa County, AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a mistrial, a second jury of the Superior Court in Maricopa County, Arizona, convicted defendant of murder, burglary, and kidnapping and returned a death verdict. Appeal was mandatory.


OVERVIEW: The Arizona Supreme Court held that the trial court did not err in declaring a mistrial after several jurors prematurely discussed the evidence. There was also no clear error in denying Batson challenges to the State's peremptory strikes of three minority jurors during selection of the second jury, because the State offered a race-neutral explanation for each strike: The State struck one juror for hardship, another for her negative feelings toward police, and the last for her criminal history. Further, other minority jurors were ultimately selected for the panel. Sufficient evidence supported a finding that the murder was "especially cruel" within the meaning of Ariz. Rev. Stat. § 13-751(F)(6); the victim almost certainly was conscious when he was tightly bound hand and foot, a pillowcase was tied over his head, and he struggled to free himself, indicating that he had time to suffer significant uncertainty as to his fate. Impact testimony from the victim's parents was properly admitted, even if the statements were not admitted to rebut specific mitigating evidence. The parents spoke of the victim's character and played the 911 call the father made after finding his son murdered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction and sentences.
